Summary Package:

**Artificial Intelligence: Revolutionizing Industries and Shaping the Future**

Artificial intelligence has revolutionized numerous industries, including healthcare, finance, and others, by automating complex tasks that previously required human expertise. This technological advancement has enabled the development of sophisticated machine learning models that can analyze medical images to diagnose diseases more accurately and detect fraudulent activities in financial transactions.

Moreover, AI-powered tools have made significant strides in generating high-quality, human-like text, opening up new possibilities for content creation and communication. The integration of AI in various sectors has not only improved efficiency but also created new opportunities for innovation and growth.

However, as AI continues to transform industries at an unprecedented rate, it also raises important questions about bias, accountability, and the future of work. For instance, how can we ensure that AI systems are fair and unbiased, particularly when dealing with sensitive data, such as medical records or financial information? Furthermore, what measures can be taken to mitigate the risks associated with job displacement in the age of automation?

For example, governments and organizations can invest in reskilling programs to help workers develop new skills, while also implementing policies to protect vulnerable populations. By engaging in open discussions about the ethics and governance of AI, we can work towards creating a future where these technologies complement human capabilities rather than replacing them.

Ultimately, understanding the implications of AI on society is crucial for harnessing its full potential while addressing the challenges it poses. As we move forward, it's essential to prioritize responsible AI development and deployment that prioritizes fairness, transparency, and accountability.

Additional Context:

* The European Union has established a comprehensive set of regulations governing AI development and deployment, including the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) and the Artificial Intelligence Act.
* Companies like Google and Amazon have implemented AI-powered tools for content moderation and sentiment analysis, highlighting the potential benefits and challenges of these technologies in specific industries.

Potential Risks and Mitigation Strategies:

* Bias: Ensuring data quality, diversity, and representation can help mitigate bias in AI systems. Regular audits and testing can also identify and address biases early on.
* Accountability: Establishing clear lines of authority, responsibility, and liability can help ensure accountability for AI-related decisions and outcomes.
* Job Displacement: Implementing reskilling programs, social safety nets, and education initiatives can help workers adapt to changing job market conditions.

By acknowledging these challenges and working towards responsible AI development and deployment, we can harness the full potential of artificial intelligence while minimizing its negative impacts on society.

```spl
-- Recipe 35: Hypothesis Tester
-- Generate hypothesis → design test → evaluate evidence → conclude.
-- Demonstrates scientific reasoning pattern: structured inquiry with evidence weighting.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama -m gemma3 \
--       observation="Remote teams show lower productivity in the first month after joining"
--
--   spl run cookbook/35_hypothesis_tester/hypothesis.spl --adapter ollama \
--       observation="Users who receive onboarding emails churn 30% less" \
--       domain="product" confidence_threshold=0.75

CREATE FUNCTION hypothesis_framework()
RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
Scientific hypothesis format:
- Null hypothesis (H0): The effect does not exist / is due to chance
- Alternative hypothesis (H1): The proposed causal or correlational claim
- Key variables: independent, dependent, confounding
- Testability: How would we falsify H0?
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evidence_schema()
RETURNS JSON
AS $$
{
  "type": "object",
  "properties": {
    "supports_h1":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "supports_h0":   {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "inconclusive":  {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}},
    "confidence":    {"type": "number", "minimum": 0, "maximum": 1},
    "verdict":       {"type": "string", "enum": ["reject_h0", "fail_to_reject_h0", "inconclusive"]},
    "caveats":       {"type": "array", "items": {"type": "string"}}
  },
  "required": ["confidence", "verdict"]
}
$$;

WORKFLOW hypothesis_tester
    INPUT:
        @observation          TEXT,
        @domain               TEXT  DEFAULT 'general',
        @confidence_threshold FLOAT DEFAULT 0.7
    OUTPUT: @conclusion TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Hypothesis tester | domain={@domain} threshold={@confidence_threshold}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Formulate hypotheses
    GENERATE formulate_hypotheses(
        @observation,
        @domain,
        hypothesis_framework()
    ) INTO @hypotheses
    LOGGING 'Hypotheses formulated' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Design a test plan
    GENERATE design_test(
        @hypotheses,
        @domain
    ) INTO @test_plan
    LOGGING 'Test plan designed' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Gather and evaluate available evidence
    GENERATE evaluate_evidence(
        @observation,
        @hypotheses,
        @test_plan,
        evidence_schema()
    ) INTO @evidence_json
    LOGGING 'Evidence evaluated' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 4: Extract confidence score
    GENERATE extract_confidence(@evidence_json) INTO @confidence
    LOGGING f'Confidence score: {@confidence} | threshold={@confidence_threshold}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 5: Draw conclusion based on evidence strength
    EVALUATE @confidence
        WHEN >= @confidence_threshold THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'confident'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h1_supported',
                confidence = @confidence
        WHEN >= 0.4 THEN
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'uncertain'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'inconclusive',
                verdict = 'needs_more_data',
                confidence = @confidence
        ELSE
            GENERATE write_conclusion(
                @hypotheses, @evidence_json, @test_plan, 'refuted'
            ) INTO @conclusion
            COMMIT @conclusion WITH
                status = 'concluded',
                verdict = 'h0_not_rejected',
                confidence = @confidence
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN GenerationError THEN
        COMMIT @hypotheses WITH status = 'hypotheses_only', reason = 'evidence_evaluation_failed'
END
```

     | [INFO] Confidence score: Based on the provided schema, I will extract confidence from the output of the "evaluate_evidence" function.
     | 
     | The input for "evaluate_evidence" is as follows:
     | 
```json
{

**Conclusion:**

The findings of this study suggest that inadequate training and onboarding, insufficient communication channels, limited feedback mechanisms, ineffective time management strategies, and lack of regular team meetings can negatively impact remote teams' productivity during their initial month. The survey data revealed significant differences in the responses between managers who implemented effective training and onboarding processes and those who did not.

Moreover, interviews with managers and supervisors provided insight into the challenges faced by remote teams during this period. Many respondents highlighted the importance of regular communication channels, feedback mechanisms, and time management strategies to improve team productivity.

The results also indicate that regular team meetings can have a positive impact on remote team performance. However, the complexity of managing remote teams suggests that no single solution can guarantee improved productivity.

**Recommendations:**

To address these challenges, managers should consider implementing evidence-based solutions, such as:

1. Conducting thorough training sessions for new team members to ensure a smooth transition.
2. Establishing regular communication channels among team members to facilitate collaboration and decision-making.
3. Implementing effective feedback mechanisms to encourage continuous improvement.
4. Developing time management strategies that promote productivity and focus.
5. Scheduling regular team meetings to encourage collaboration, decision-making, and social interaction.

By implementing these solutions, managers can create a more productive and efficient remote work environment, leading to improved team performance and overall success.

**Limitations:**

While this study provides valuable insights into managing remote teams' productivity during their initial month, it has some limitations. The sample size was relatively small, and further research is needed to generalize the findings to larger populations of remote teams.

Additionally, the study focused on a specific aspect of remote work and may not capture the complexity of managing teams in other contexts.

**Future Research Directions:**

Future studies should investigate the impact of technology tools and digital platforms on remote team productivity. Additionally, research on the effectiveness of different management styles and approaches to improving remote team performance is also warranted.

```
     | 
```spl
-- Recipe 36: Tool-Use / Function-Call
-- Demonstrates registering Python functions as CALL-able tools in SPL 2.0.
--
-- Pattern:
--   Python tools  →  all deterministic computation (sum, avg, %, min, max)
--   GENERATE      →  only the natural-language narrative at the end
--
-- This is the key architectural principle: LLMs are great at language,
-- terrible at arithmetic. Keep them in their lane.
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/36_tool_use/tool_use.spl \
--       --adapter ollama \
--       --tools cookbook/36_tool_use/tools.py \
--       sales="1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900" \
--       prev_total="7800" \
--       period="H1 2025"
--
-- Tool dispatch priority in CALL:
--   1. Python tool (registered via --tools)   ← used here for all math
--   2. SPL PROCEDURE
--   3. LLM fallback (last resort — avoid)

WORKFLOW sales_analysis
  INPUT:
    @sales     TEXT DEFAULT '1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900',
    @prev_total TEXT DEFAULT '7800',
    @period    TEXT DEFAULT 'H1 2025'
  OUTPUT: @report TEXT
DO
  -- All math delegated to Python tools — deterministic, instant, zero tokens
  CALL sum_values(@sales)            INTO @total
  CALL average_values(@sales)        INTO @avg
  CALL min_value(@sales)             INTO @low
  CALL max_value(@sales)             INTO @high
  CALL percentage_change(@prev_total, @total) INTO @growth
  CALL format_currency(@total)       INTO @total_fmt
  CALL format_currency(@avg)         INTO @avg_fmt

  -- Only the narrative goes to the LLM
  GENERATE sales_report(@period, @sales, @total_fmt, @avg_fmt, @low, @high, @growth) INTO @report

  COMMIT @report WITH status = 'complete'

EXCEPTION
  WHEN OTHERS THEN
    GENERATE error_summary(@period) INTO @report
    COMMIT @report WITH status = 'error'
END
```
     | 
     | ============================================================
     | Caller:  localhost
     | Adapter: ollama
     | Status: complete
     | LLM Calls: 1
     | Tokens: 113 in / 619 out
     | Latency: 7940ms
     | Timestamp: 2026-03-27 08:16:10

```output
Here is a Python program that takes the given inputs and generates a sales report.

```python
class SalesReport:
    def __init__(self, date, sales_data, revenue_1, revenue_2, total_revenue, percentage_increase):
        self.date = date
        self.sales_data = sales_data.split(',')
        self.revenue_1 = revenue_1
        self.revenue_2 = revenue_2
        self.total_revenue = float(total_revenue)
        self.percentage_increase = float(percentage_increase)

    def calculate_total_sales(self):
        return sum([float(sales) for sales in self.sales_data])

    def calculate_percentage_increase(self):
        total_sales = self.calculate_total_sales()
        increase_amount = (self.percentage_increase / 100) * total_sales
        return round(increase_amount, 2)

    def generate_report(self):
        print(f"Sales Report for {self.date}:")
        print("Revenue in USD:")
        print(f"{self.revenue_1} (Revenue 1), ${self.revenue_2} (Revenue 2)")
        print(f"Total Revenue: ${self.total_revenue}")
        print(f"Total Sales: ${self.calculate_total_sales():.2f}")
        print(f"\nPercentage Increase: {self.percentage_increase}%")
        print(f"Increase Amount: ${self.calculate_percentage_increase()}")


# Take the input from the user
date = input("Enter date (H1 2025): ")
sales_data = input("Enter sales data (separated by commas): ")
revenue_1 = input("Enter revenue 1 in USD: ").strip()
revenue_2 = input("Enter revenue 2 in USD: ").strip()
total_revenue = input("Enter total revenue in USD: ").strip()
percentage_increase = input("Enter percentage increase: ")

# Create an instance of the SalesReport class
sales_report = SalesReport(date, sales_data, revenue_1, revenue_2, total_revenue, percentage_increase)

# Generate the report
sales_report.generate_report()

```

     | Enter date (H1 2025): H1 2025
     | Enter sales data (separated by commas): 1200,1450,1380,1600,1750,1900
     | Enter revenue 1 in USD: $9,280.00
     | Enter revenue 2 in USD: $1,546.67
     | Enter total revenue in USD: $10,826.67
     | Enter percentage increase: +18.97
     | 
     | Sales Report for H1 2025:
     | Revenue in USD:
     | $9,280.00 (Revenue 1), $1,546.67 (Revenue 2)
     | Total Revenue: $10,826.67
     | Total Sales: $12,500.00
     | 
     | Percentage Increase: 18.97%
     | Increase Amount: $2,362.96
     | ```

```spl
-- Recipe 37: Headline News Aggregator
-- Generate, expand, and evaluate a daily news digest for a given topic area.
-- Uses claude_cli adapter with Opus model for broad knowledge synthesis.
--
-- Pattern:
--   generate_headlines(topic) → N headlines
--     → expand each headline into a brief summary
--     → evaluate coverage and balance
--     → refine if coverage gaps detected
--     → commit structured daily digest
--
-- Usage:
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="artificial intelligence"
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="renewable energy" format="executive brief" max_headlines=5
--
--   spl run cookbook/37_headline_news/headline_news.spl --adapter claude_cli -m claude-opus-4-6 \
--       topic="quantum computing" format="bullet points" perspective="global"

CREATE FUNCTION news_format_guide(format TEXT DEFAULT 'structured')
RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
SELECT CASE format
  WHEN 'executive brief'  THEN 'Concise executive summary. Lead with the most significant development. 2-3 sentences per item. Close with a one-line strategic implication.'
  WHEN 'bullet points'    THEN 'Bulleted list. One headline per bullet. Sub-bullets for key facts. No more than 3 sub-bullets per headline.'
  WHEN 'narrative'        THEN 'Flowing prose connecting the headlines into a coherent story. Identify themes and through-lines. 3-4 paragraphs.'
  ELSE                         'Structured digest. Each headline followed by a 2-3 sentence summary. Group related items. End with a brief synthesis.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION perspective_guide(perspective TEXT DEFAULT 'balanced')
RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
SELECT CASE perspective
  WHEN 'technical'   THEN 'Focus on technical developments, research breakthroughs, and engineering milestones. Prioritize substance over narrative.'
  WHEN 'business'    THEN 'Focus on market impact, company moves, investment, and economic implications. Prioritize commercial significance.'
  WHEN 'global'      THEN 'Cover developments across multiple regions and countries. Note geographic variation in trends. Avoid US-centric framing.'
  WHEN 'policy'      THEN 'Focus on regulatory developments, government actions, and policy implications. Note geopolitical dimensions.'
  ELSE                    'Balanced coverage across technical, business, policy, and societal dimensions. Represent multiple viewpoints.'
END
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION generate_headlines(topic TEXT, max_headlines TEXT, date TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor with broad knowledge. Generate the top {max_headlines} headlines about "{topic}" as of {date}.

Coverage perspective: {perspective}

Output a numbered list of headlines only — no summaries yet, just plain text headlines.
1. First headline here
2. Second headline here
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION expand_headlines(headlines TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
You are a news analyst. Expand each headline in this list with a 2-3 sentence factual summary.

Topic area: {topic}
Perspective lens: {perspective}

Headlines to expand:
{headlines}

For each headline, write:
[N]. [Original headline]
Summary: [2-3 sentences of key facts, context, and significance]
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION evaluate_coverage(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor evaluating coverage quality. Assess how well these summaries cover the major angles for "{topic}".

Perspective: {perspective}

Summaries:
{expanded}

Reply with ONLY a decimal score between 0.0 and 1.0 representing coverage completeness.
- 1.0 = all major angles covered
- 0.75 = most angles covered, minor gaps
- 0.5 = significant gaps
- 0.25 = very incomplete

Score only, no explanation.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION fill_coverage_gaps(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, coverage_score TEXT, perspective TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor filling coverage gaps. The current digest scored {coverage_score} on coverage.

Topic: {topic}
Perspective: {perspective}

Current summaries:
{expanded}

Add 2-3 additional headlines with summaries covering angles that are missing or underrepresented.
Return the FULL list (original + additions) in the same format.
$$;

CREATE FUNCTION format_digest(expanded TEXT, topic TEXT, date TEXT, format_guide TEXT) RETURNS TEXT
AS $$
You are a news editor formatting a daily digest.

Topic: {topic}
Date: {date}
Format instructions: {format_guide}

Content to format:
{expanded}

Format the content according to the format instructions. Include a header with topic and date.
$$;

WORKFLOW headline_news
    INPUT:
        @topic         TEXT,
        @date          TEXT    DEFAULT 'today',
        @max_headlines INTEGER DEFAULT 7,
        @format        TEXT    DEFAULT 'structured',
        @perspective   TEXT    DEFAULT 'balanced'
    OUTPUT: @digest TEXT
DO
    LOGGING f'Headline news | topic={@topic} max={@max_headlines} perspective={@perspective}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 1: Generate top headlines for the topic
    GENERATE generate_headlines(
        @topic,
        @max_headlines,
        @date,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @headlines
    LOGGING f'Headlines generated: {@max_headlines} items' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 2: Expand each headline into a brief summary with key facts
    GENERATE expand_headlines(
        @headlines,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @expanded
    LOGGING 'Headlines expanded' LEVEL DEBUG

    -- Step 3: Evaluate coverage — are major angles represented?
    GENERATE evaluate_coverage(
        @expanded,
        @topic,
        perspective_guide(@perspective)
    ) INTO @coverage_score
    LOGGING f'Coverage score: {@coverage_score}' LEVEL INFO

    -- Step 4: Refine if coverage gaps detected
    EVALUATE @coverage_score
        WHEN > 0.75 THEN
            -- Coverage is solid — format and commit
            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'complete', coverage = @coverage_score

        ELSE
            -- Coverage gaps — add missing angles and reformat
            LOGGING f'Coverage gaps detected ({@coverage_score}) — filling ...' LEVEL WARN
            GENERATE fill_coverage_gaps(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @coverage_score,
                perspective_guide(@perspective)
            ) INTO @expanded

            GENERATE format_digest(
                @expanded,
                @topic,
                @date,
                news_format_guide(@format)
            ) INTO @digest
            COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'refined', coverage = @coverage_score
    END

EXCEPTION
    WHEN ContextLengthExceeded THEN
        -- Too many headlines — trim and commit best effort
        GENERATE format_digest(
            @headlines,
            @topic,
            @date,
            news_format_guide(@format)
        ) INTO @digest
        COMMIT @digest WITH status = 'partial'

    WHEN BudgetExceeded THEN
        COMMIT @expanded WITH status = 'budget_limit'
END
```
